_**User**_

# Jekyll to Astro Migration Prompt

I need you to help me migrate my Jekyll blog to Astro + TypeScript + Cloudflare Pages. This is a complex migration with several custom components that need special handling.

## Project Context

- **Source**: Jekyll blog at `~/code/antgonzales.github.io` (GitHub Pages)
- **Target**: Current directory (Astro site already scaffolded)
- **Stack**: Astro + TypeScript + Cloudflare Pages
- **Constraint**: I want to do this entirely through prompts - no manual coding

## Key Migration Challenges

### 1. Custom Markdown Syntax

My Jekyll blog uses specific markdown extensions that need to be handled in Astro:

**Kramdown attribute syntax:**

- `{:target="_blank"}` - Link attributes (e.g., `[Product Engineer](https://leerob.com/n/product-engineers){:target="_blank"}`)
- `{:toc}` - Table of contents generation
- Other kramdown-style attributes applied to elements

**Content break syntax:**

- `<!--break-->` - Separates excerpt content (shown on index) from full content (shown only on individual post pages)

**Example usage:**

```markdown
This is my post excerpt that appears on the index page.

<!--break-->

This content only appears on the full post page, not in the excerpt.

Check out this [external link](https://example.com){:target="\_blank"} that opens in a new tab.

{:toc}
```

### 2. Feed.xml Route

- Current Jekyll generates `/feed.xml` for RSS
- Need equivalent RSS feed generation in Astro
- Should maintain same URL structure and XML format

### 3. Custom Jekyll/Ruby Tags

- `{{ site.time }}` - Current timestamp
- `{{ page.date | date: "%B %d, %Y" }}` - Date formatting
- `{{ content | excerpt }}` - Post excerpts
- `{{ page.tags | join: ", " }}` - Tag lists

## Migration Tasks

### Phase 1: Analysis & Setup

1. **Analyze Jekyll structure** at `~/code/antgonzales.github.io`
2. **Examine repository files**: \_config.yml, layouts, includes, posts, and custom components
3. **Review existing Astro setup** at the target location
4. **Plan migration strategy** based on both codebases
5. **Configure Cloudflare Pages** deployment settings

### Phase 2: Content Migration

1. **Convert Jekyll front matter** to Astro format
2. **Handle kramdown attribute syntax** (`{:target="_blank"}`, `{:toc}`)
3. **Process content breaks** (`<!--break-->`) for excerpt handling
4. **Migrate blog posts** maintaining URL structure and excerpt functionality
5. **Handle static assets** (images, CSS, etc.)

### Phase 3: Feature Recreation

1. **Recreate RSS feed** at `/feed.xml`
2. **Convert Jekyll templates** to Astro layouts
3. **Implement kramdown attribute equivalents** (link targets, TOC generation)
4. **Set up excerpt handling** based on `<!--break-->` markers
5. **Implement custom Ruby tag equivalents**
6. **Set up pagination** for blog posts

### Phase 4: Testing & Validation

Use Playwright MCP to:

1. **Visual regression testing** - Compare old vs new pages
2. **Content verification** - Ensure all posts migrated correctly
3. **RSS feed validation** - Check XML structure and content
4. **Performance testing** - Lighthouse scores
5. **Link checking** - Verify all internal/external links work

## Success Criteria

- [ ] All blog posts render identically to Jekyll version
- [ ] Kramdown attributes work (`:target="_blank"`, `:toc`, etc.)
- [ ] Content breaks (`<!--break-->`) properly separate excerpts
- [ ] RSS feed generates correctly at `/feed.xml`
- [ ] All Jekyll/Ruby tags have Astro equivalents
- [ ] Site builds and deploys to Cloudflare Pages
- [ ] Performance score >= 90 on Lighthouse
- [ ] No broken links or missing content

## My Approach

1. **Start with analysis** - I'll share my Jekyll files
2. **Iterate through prompts** - Each phase gets its own prompt
3. **Test continuously** - Use Playwright to verify each step
4. **Refine based on results** - Fix issues through prompt refinement

## First Step

Please start by thoroughly analyzing the Jekyll blog repository at:
**`~/code/antgonzales.github.io`**

Examine the complete repository structure, including:

- `_config.yml` configuration
- `_layouts/` and `_includes/` directories
- Sample blog posts in `_posts/`
- Any custom plugins or components
- Static assets and styling

Then create a detailed migration plan that accounts for my custom Markdown tags, RSS feed, and Jekyll/Ruby template tags. What patterns do you see that need special handling?

---

**Note**: I'll be documenting this entire process for a blog post about "vibe coding" - migrating a blog using only AI prompts. Your responses will help demonstrate effective prompt engineering for complex development tasks.

     2‚Üílayout: post
     3‚Üítitle: "How to test React Router components with Testing Library"
     4‚Üídescription: "Discover why avoiding mocks in Jest enhances testing. Learn
     5‚Üístrategies for resilient, standards-based tests that improve code
     6‚Üímaintainability and reliability."
     7‚Üídate: 2024-06-03
     8‚Üílast_modified_at: 2024-09-29
     9‚Üíredirect_from:
    10‚Üí- /blog/dont-mock-in-jest.html
    11‚Üí---
    12‚Üí
    13‚ÜíLet's test React Router components with Jest.
    14‚Üí
    15‚Üí* Do not remove this line (it will not be displayed)
    16‚Üí{:toc}
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üí<!--break-->
    19‚Üí
    20‚Üí## Testing navigation elements in React
    21‚Üí
    22‚ÜíReact Testing Library's [React Router
    23‚Üíexample](https://testing-library.com/docs/example-react-router/) shows how to
    24‚Üítest routing at the root component level, however, it doesn't provide guidance
    25‚Üíon children components. I came across the example below in a recent code
    26‚Üíreview. Our team uses a [custom test
    27‚Üírender](https://testing-library.com/docs/react-testing-library/setup/#custom-render)
    28‚Üíto help with components that utilize React Providers, including `MemoryRouter`.
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí\```jsx
    31‚Üíimport { render } from '@testing-library/react';
    32‚Üíimport React from 'react';
    33‚Üíimport { MemoryRouter, Route, Routes } from 'react-router-dom';
    34‚Üí
    35‚Üífunction renderWithProviders(
    36‚Üí  ui,
    37‚Üí  {
    38‚Üí    initialRouterEntries = ['/'],
    39‚Üí    route = '/',
    40‚Üí    ...renderOptions
    41‚Üí  } = {}
    42‚Üí) {
    43‚Üí  const Wrapper = ({ children }) => (
    44‚Üí    <MemoryRouter initialEntries={initialRouterEntries}>
    45‚Üí      <Routes>
    46‚Üí        <Route path={route} element={children} />
    47‚Üí      </Routes>
    48‚Üí    </MemoryRouter>
    49‚Üí  );
    50‚Üí
    51‚Üí  return {
    52‚Üí    ...render(ui, { wrapper: Wrapper, ...renderOptions }),
    53‚Üí  };
    54‚Üí}
    55‚Üí 
    56‚Üíexport * from '@testing-library/react'  
    57‚Üí   
    58‚Üíexport { renderWithProviders };
    59‚Üí\```
    60‚Üí
    61‚Üí\```jsx
    62‚Üíimport { fireEvent, renderWithProviders, screen } from '@/testUtils';
    63‚Üíimport React from 'react';
    64‚Üí
    65‚Üíjest.mock('react-router-dom', () => ({
    66‚Üí  ...jest.requireActual('react-router-dom'),
    67‚Üí  // ‚ùå Mocking React Router's hook
    68‚Üí  useNavigate: () => mockedUseNavigate,
    69‚Üí}));
    70‚Üí
    71‚Üídescribe('<ComponentWithNavigation />', () => {
    72‚Üí  it('provides a link to return to the dashboard', async () => {
    73‚Üí    renderWithProviders(<ComponentWithNavigation />)
    74‚Üí    const link = screen.getByRole(link, {name: 'Go to Home'});
    75‚Üí    fireEvent.click(link);
    76‚Üí    // ‚ùå Testing implementation details
    77‚Üí    expect(mockedUseNavigate).toHaveBeenCalledWith('/', expect.anything());
    78‚Üí  });
    79‚Üí});
    80‚Üí\```
    81‚Üí
    82‚ÜíAlthough this approach tests the behavior of our component, it also checks the
    83‚Üíimplementation details of React Router and does not utilize HTML
    84‚Üíspecifications. Imagine the following scenario:
    85‚Üí
    86‚Üí* We continue with the test suite checking the  `useNavigation()` hook and
    87‚Üí  write all of our tests going forward in this way
    88‚Üí* React Router releases a new version that alters the behavior of
    89‚Üí  `useNavigation()` or deprecates the hook entirely
    90‚Üí* We perform the upgrade without fully understanding the implications
    91‚Üí* The test suite pass on CI/CD
    92‚Üí* Production fails üí•
    93‚Üí
    94‚ÜíBy binding our test suite to the implementation details of React Router, we've
    95‚Üíremoved our ability to check that the integration between our code and the
    96‚Üídependency work correctly.  We've opened ourselves up to false positives or
    97‚Üífalse negatives in our test suite.
    98‚Üí
    99‚ÜíA better, and simpler, approach is to check the `<a/>` tag's `href` property.
   100‚Üí
   101‚Üí\```jsx
   102‚Üíimport { render, screen } from '@/testUtils';
   103‚Üíimport React from 'react';
   104‚Üí
   105‚Üídescribe('<ComponentWithNavigation />', () => {
   106‚Üí  it('provides a link to return to the dashboard', async () => {
   107‚Üí    renderWithProviders(<ComponentWithNavigation />)
   108‚Üí    const link = screen.getByRole(link, {name: 'Go to Home'});
   109‚Üí    // ‚úÖ Checking the link element render
   110‚Üí    expect(link.href).toBe('/');
   111‚Üí  });
   112‚Üí});
   113‚Üí\```
   114‚Üí
   115‚ÜíWe've now reduced the brittleness of the test and created more streamlined
   116‚Üíapproach to checking the navigation of the component without the custom test
   117‚Üírender.
   118‚Üí
   119‚Üí## Conclusion
   120‚Üí
   121‚ÜíEffective testing in React applications is not just about covering every line
   122‚Üíof code with tests; it's about writing tests that remain resilient against
   123‚Üíchange. The goal of testing is not only to catch errors before they reach
   124‚Üíproduction but to provide a safety net that allows for confident refactoring
   125‚Üíand upgrades. By focusing on the user's perspective and the external interface
   126‚Üíof components, rather than the underlying implementation, we ensure that our
   127‚Üítests are both meaningful and durable.
   128‚Üí
```

Result:

```
1‚Üí{% capture headingsWorkspace %}
     2‚Üí  {% comment %}
     3‚Üí    Version 1.0.3
     4‚Üí      https://github.com/allejo/jekyll-anchor-headings
     5‚Üí
     6‚Üí    "Be the pull request you wish to see in the world." ~Ben Balter
     7‚Üí
     8‚Üí    Usage:
     9‚Üí      {% include anchor_headings.html html=content %}
    10‚Üí
    11‚Üí    Parameters:
    12‚Üí      * html          (string) - the HTML of compiled markdown generated by kramdown in Jekyll
    13‚Üí
    14‚Üí    Optional Parameters:
    15‚Üí      * beforeHeading (bool)   : false  - Set to true if the anchor should be placed _before_ the heading's content
    16‚Üí      * anchorBody    (string) :  ''    - The content that will be placed inside the anchor; the `%heading%` placeholder is available
    17‚Üí      * anchorClass   (string) :  ''    - The class(es) that will be used for each anchor. Separate multiple classes with a space
    18‚Üí      * anchorTitle   (string) :  ''    - The `title` attribute that will be used for anchors
    19‚Üí      * h_min         (int)    :  1     - The minimum header level to build an anchor for; any header lower than this value will be ignored
    20‚Üí      * h_max         (int)    :  6     - The maximum header level to build an anchor for; any header greater than this value will be ignored
    21‚Üí      * bodyPrefix    (string) :  ''    - Anything that should be inserted inside of the heading tag _before_ its anchor and content
    22‚Üí      * bodySuffix    (string) :  ''    - Anything that should be inserted inside of the heading tag _after_ its anchor and content
    23‚Üí
    24‚Üí    Output:
    25‚Üí      The original HTML with the addition of anchors inside of all of the h1-h6 headings.
    26‚Üí  {% endcomment %}
    27‚Üí
    28‚Üí  {% assign minHeader = include.h_min | default: 1 %}
    29‚Üí  {% assign maxHeader = include.h_max | default: 6 %}
    30‚Üí  {% assign beforeHeading = include.beforeHeading %}
    31‚Üí  {% assign nodes = include.html | split: '<h' %}
    32‚Üí
    33‚Üí  {% capture edited_headings %}{% endcapture %}
    34‚Üí
    35‚Üí  {% for _node in nodes %}
    36‚Üí    {% capture node %}{{ _node | strip }}{% endcapture %}
    37‚Üí
    38‚Üí    {% if node == "" %}
    39‚Üí      {% continue %}
    40‚Üí    {% endif %}
    41‚Üí
    42‚Üí    {% assign nextChar = node | replace: '"', '' | strip | slice: 0, 1 %}
    43‚Üí    {% assign headerLevel = nextChar | times: 1 %}
    44‚Üí
    45‚Üí    <!-- If the level is cast to 0, it means it's not a h1-h6 tag, so let's try to fix it -->
    46‚Üí    {% if headerLevel == 0 %}
    47‚Üí      {% if nextChar != '<' and nextChar != '' %}
    48‚Üí        {% capture node %}<h{{ node }}{% endcapture %}
    49‚Üí      {% endif %}
    50‚Üí
    51‚Üí      {% capture edited_headings %}{{ edited_headings }}{{ node }}{% endcapture %}
    52‚Üí      {% continue %}
    53‚Üí    {% endif %}
    54‚Üí
    55‚Üí    {% assign _workspace = node | split: '</h' %}
    56‚Üí    {% assign _idWorkspace = _workspace[0] | split: 'id="' %}
    57‚Üí    {% assign _idWorkspace = _idWorkspace[1] | split: '"' %}
    58‚Üí    {% assign html_id = _idWorkspace[0] %}
    59‚Üí
    60‚Üí    {% capture _hAttrToStrip %}{{ _workspace[0] | split: '>' | first }}>{% endcapture %}
    61‚Üí    {% assign header = _workspace[0] | replace: _hAttrToStrip, '' %}
    62‚Üí
    63‚Üí    <!-- Build the anchor to inject for our heading -->
    64‚Üí    {% capture anchor %}{% endcapture %}
    65‚Üí
    66‚Üí    {% if html_id and headerLevel >= minHeader and headerLevel <= maxHeader %}
    67‚Üí      {% capture anchor %}href="#{{ html_id}}"{% endcapture %}
    68‚Üí
    69‚Üí      {% if include.anchorClass %}
    70‚Üí        {% capture anchor %}{{ anchor }} class="{{ include.anchorClass }}"{% endcapture %}
    71‚Üí      {% endif %}
    72‚Üí
    73‚Üí      {% if include.anchorTitle %}
    74‚Üí        {% capture anchor %}{{ anchor }} title="{{ include.anchorTitle | replace: '%heading%', header }}"{% endcapture %}
    75‚Üí      {% endif %}
    76‚Üí
    77‚Üí      {% capture anchor %}<a {{ anchor }}>{{ include.anchorBody | replace: '%heading%', header | default: '' }}</a>{% endcapture %}
    78‚Üí
    79‚Üí      <!-- In order to prevent adding extra space after a heading, we'll let the 'anchor' value contain it -->
    80‚Üí      {% if beforeHeading %}
    81‚Üí        {% capture anchor %}{{ anchor }} {% endcapture %}
    82‚Üí      {% else %}
    83‚Üí        {% capture anchor %} {{ anchor }}{% endcapture %}
    84‚Üí      {% endif %}
    85‚Üí    {% endif %}
    86‚Üí
    87‚Üí    {% capture new_heading %}
    88‚Üí      <h{{ _hAttrToStrip }}
    89‚Üí        {{ include.bodyPrefix }}
    90‚Üí        {% if beforeHeading %}
    91‚Üí          {{ anchor }}{{ header }}
    92‚Üí        {% else %}
    93‚Üí          {{ header }}{{ anchor }}
    94‚Üí        {% endif %}
    95‚Üí        {{ include.bodySuffix }}
    96‚Üí      </h{{ _workspace | last }}
    97‚Üí    {% endcapture %}
    98‚Üí    {% capture edited_headings %}{{ edited_headings }}{{ new_heading }}{% endcapture %}
    99‚Üí  {% endfor %}
   100‚Üí{% endcapture %}{% assign headingsWorkspace = '' %}{{ edited_headings | strip }}
   101‚Üí
```

## Migration Plan

### Phase 1: Kramdown Processing Setup
1. **Install remark plugins** for kramdown attribute processing
2. **Create custom remark plugin** to handle `{:target="_blank"}` syntax
3. **Implement TOC generation** for `{:toc}` markers
4. **Set up excerpt separation** based on `<!--break-->` markers

### Phase 2: Content Architecture
1. **Create Astro content collections** for blog posts
2. **Convert Jekyll layouts** to Astro layouts (default.html, post.html)
3. **Migrate Jekyll includes** to Astro components (header, footer, head)
4. **Implement anchor headings** equivalent to anchor_headings.html

### Phase 3: Template Features
1. **Recreate Jekyll liquid filters** (`date`, `excerpt`)
2. **Implement RSS feed** at `/feed.xml` route
3. **Add pagination** for blog listing
4. **Port Jekyll front matter** to Astro format

### Phase 4: Special Handling Required
- **Kramdown attributes**: Need custom remark plugin
- **Content breaks**: Custom excerpt processing
- **Auto-linking headers**: Port anchor_headings.html logic
- **Date formatting**: Recreate Jekyll's date filters
- **URL structure**: Maintain `/blog/:title` permalinks

The migration requires careful handling of your custom Kramdown syntax and content break patterns. Your blog has sophisticated features that need equivalent Astro implementations.

Ready to proceed with Phase 1?

1‚Üí---
     2‚Üílayout: post
     3‚Üítitle: "How to improve Git monorepo performance"
     4‚Üídescription: "Optimize Git in monorepos with an optimized Git config. Follow
     5‚Üíclear steps to boost CPU performance and workflow efficiency"
     6‚Üídate: 2023-12-15
     7‚Üílast_modified_at: 2024-05-04
     8‚Üí---
     9‚Üí[Git v2.37.0](https://github.blog/2022-06-27-highlights-from-git-2-37/)
    10‚Üíintroduced new features that significantly improve performance for repositories
    11‚Üíwith large numbers of files. This blog post will cover custom Git monorepo
    12‚Üíconfigurations to improve local performance and provide step-by-step guidance
    13‚Üíto rollback if anything goes wrong. We‚Äôll look into these new features and
    14‚Üíexplain how to implement them effectively in your global or local Git config.
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí* Do not remove this line (it will not be displayed)
    17‚Üí{:toc}
    18‚Üí
    19‚Üí<!--break-->
    20‚Üí
    21‚Üí## Quickstart
    22‚Üí
    23‚Üí<div class="callout warning-callout">
    24‚Üí  <p>
    25‚Üí    <strong>Warning:</strong> Upgrade Git to 2.42.0+ and perform the steps in
    26‚Üí    this tutorial on your main branch. `index.skipHash` causes errors on older
    27‚Üí    Git versions.
    28‚Üí  </p>
    29‚Üí</div>
    30‚Üí
    31‚Üí### Create a custom Git config file at `~/.gitconfig.monorepo`
    32‚Üí
    33‚Üí\```ini
    34‚Üí[core]
    35‚Üí    commitgraph = true
    36‚Üí    fsmonitor = true
    37‚Üí    writeCommitGraph = true
    38‚Üí[feature]
    39‚Üí    manyFiles = true
    40‚Üí\```
    41‚Üí
    42‚Üí### Include the custom configuration in your global or local Git config
    43‚Üí
    44‚Üí\```ini
    45‚Üí[include]
    46‚Üí    path = ~/.gitconfig.monorepo
    47‚Üí[user]
    48‚Üí    email = 123345+darth.vader@users.noreply.github.com
    49‚Üí    name = Darth Vader
    50‚Üí[init]
    51‚Üí    defaultBranch = main
    52‚Üí[core]
    53‚Üí    editor = nvim
    54‚Üí[color]
    55‚Üí    ui = auto
    56‚Üí[branch]
    57‚Üí    autosetuprebase = always
    58‚Üí[rebase]
    59‚Üí    autoStash = true
    60‚Üí[pull]
    61‚Üí    rebase = true
    62‚Üí[push]
    63‚Üí    default = current
    64‚Üí\```
    65‚Üí
    66‚Üí### Update Git index to version 4 in repo
    67‚Üí
    68‚ÜíAlthough `feature.manyFiles` sets the default index version, you need to
    69‚Üímanually update the [index format](https://git-scm.com/docs/index-format) on
    70‚Üíyour local repository through your terminal.
    71‚Üí
    72‚Üí\```console
    73‚Üí$ cd ~/example-monorepo
    74‚Üí$ git update-index --index-version 4
    75‚Üí\```
    76‚Üí### Start `fsmonitor‚Äîdaemon`
    77‚Üí
    78‚Üí\```console
    79‚Üí$ cd ~/example-monorepo
    80‚Üí$ git fsmonitor--daemon start
    81‚Üí\```
    82‚Üí
    83‚Üí## Results
    84‚Üí
    85‚ÜíUsing the custom Git configuration and updated index format, my command
    86‚Üíexecution time for "git status" was reduced from approximately 0.316 seconds to
    87‚Üí0.118 seconds, and by a decrease in CPU utilization from 425% to 89%,
    88‚Üíleading to a significantly improved performance. Additionally, I no longer
    89‚Üíencounter `fatal: Unable to create 'project_path/.git/index.lock': File
    90‚Üíexists.` errors while performing basic Git commands (MacOS Intel Core i9).
    91‚Üí
    92‚Üí**Before**
    93‚Üí\```console
    94‚Üí$ time git status
    95‚ÜíOn branch main
    96‚ÜíYour branch is up to date with 'origin/main'.
    97‚Üí
    98‚Üínothing to commit, working tree clean
    99‚Üígit status  0.21s user 1.14s system 425% cpu 0.316 total
   100‚Üí\```
   101‚Üí
   102‚Üí**After**
   103‚Üí\```console
   104‚Üí$ time git status
   105‚ÜíOn branch main
   106‚ÜíYour branch is up to date with 'origin/main'.
   107‚Üí
   108‚Üínothing to commit, working tree clean
   109‚Üígit status  0.08s user 0.02s system 89% cpu 0.118 total
   110‚Üí\```
   111‚Üí
   112‚Üí## Explanation of configurations
   113‚Üí
   114‚Üí**`feature.manyFiles`**
   115‚Üí
   116‚ÜíOptimizes repositories with large numbers of files and commit histories.
   117‚ÜíEnabling this configuration option enables the following by default:
   118‚Üí
   119‚Üí* `index.skipHash=true`
   120‚Üí* `index.version=4`
   121‚Üí* `core.untrackedCache=true`
   122‚Üí
   123‚ÜíGit writes an entirely new index in `index.lock` and then replaces `.git/index`
   124‚Üíwhen you use basic commands. In a monorepo with many files, this index can be
   125‚Üílarge and take several seconds to write every time you perform a command.
   126‚ÜíUpgrading from the standard version 2 to version 4 reduces index size by 30% to
   127‚Üí50% by compressing the pathnames, which results in faster load time on
   128‚Üíoperations. Caching untracked files adds more memory load but again reduces the
   129‚Üíload time.
   130‚Üí
   131‚ÜíWhen performing simple Git commands, I would encounter the following errors
   132‚Üíbefore I made the update:
   133‚Üí
   134‚Üí\```console
   135‚Üífatal: Unable to create 'project_path/.git/index.lock': File exists.
   136‚Üí\```
   137‚Üí
   138‚Üí**`core.commitgraph`**
   139‚Üí
   140‚ÜíGit will use a commit history cache to significantly speed up history
   141‚Üíoperations, such as `git log` with the `--graph` option.
   142‚Üí
   143‚Üí**`fetch.writeCommitGraph`**
   144‚Üí
   145‚ÜíImproves performance of commands like `git push -f` and `git log --graph` by
   146‚Üíwriting a commit-graph on every `git fetch`.
   147‚Üí
   148‚Üí## How to revert changes
   149‚Üí
   150‚ÜíIn the event that you experience an error or issues with your Git operations,
   151‚Üírevert the changes by doing the following:
   152‚Üí
   153‚Üí1. Update global or local Git config:
   154‚Üí    * Open your global or local Git config file.
   155‚Üí    * Remove or comment out the include path for the custom configuration.
   156‚Üí2. Revert index version in repo:
   157‚Üí    * Go to the specific repository (e.g., `cd ~/example-monorepo`).
   158‚Üí    * If you want to revert the index version to a previous state (e.g.,
   159‚Üí       version 2), run the following command: `git update-index --index-version
   160‚Üí       2`
   161‚Üí    * Note: This step depends on your requirements and the original index
   162‚Üí       version you were using.
   163‚Üí3. Stop fsmonitor daemon in repo:
   164‚Üí    * In the repository where you started the `fsmonitor--daemon`, stop it
   165‚Üí       using `git fsmonitor--daemon stop`
   166‚Üí    * This will disable the file system monitor for that repository.
   167‚Üí4. General check and cleanup:
   168‚Üí    * Run `git status` to ensure that Git is working properly.
   169‚Üí
   170‚Üí## References
   171‚Üí
   172‚Üí* [How to Improve Performance in Git: The Complete
   173‚Üí  Guide](https://www.git-tower.com/blog/git-performance/)
   174‚Üí* [Improve Git monorepo performance with a file system
   175‚Üí  monitor](https://github.blog/2022-06-29-improve-git-monorepo-performance-with-a-file-system-monitor/)
   176‚Üí* [git error `invalid data in index` with index.skipHash
   177‚Üí  config](https://github.com/rust-lang/cargo/issues/11857)
   178‚Üí* [git 2.40.0 index.skipHash incompatible with
   179‚Üí  libgit2](https://github.com/libgit2/libgit2/issues/6531)
   180‚Üí
   181‚Üí
```

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514) (sidechain)**_

Tool use: **Read** `/Users/anthonygonzales/code/antgonzales.github.io/_posts/2020-04-21-why-learn-test-driven-development.md`

```
1‚Üí---
     2‚Üílayout: post
     3‚Üítitle: "Why learn Test-Driven Development?"
     4‚Üídescription: "Create a safe environment to take risks, build confidence, and write legible code. Learn how to start with Javascript, React"
     5‚Üíimage: "glass-house-at-night-compressed.jpg"
     6‚Üídate: 2020-04-21
     7‚Üí---
     8‚Üí
     9‚ÜíAcross all of my professional software projects, I insist on Test-Driven
    10‚ÜíDevelopment (TDD). Not all developers share my enthusiasm and some see testing
    11‚Üías onerous and costly. There's so much to learn, you have to maintain a whole
    12‚Üíset of dependencies and libraries, you have to mock dependencies, it takes too
    13‚Üílong, and the list goes on. These concerns are cultural and have less to do with
    14‚Üíproficiency. TDD is another skill to learn and a powerful tool for the long term
    15‚Üíhealth of a software project. Test-Driven Development creates a safe environment
    16‚Üífor developers to take risks, builds trust between team members and management,
    17‚Üíand provides legibility for other developers to make changes.
    18‚Üí
    19‚Üí* Do not remove this line (it will not be displayed)
    20‚Üí{:toc}
    21‚Üí
    22‚Üí<!--break-->
    23‚Üí
    24‚Üí## Safe danger
    25‚Üí
    26‚Üí![Philip Johnson's Glass House at night](/assets/img/glass-house-at-night-compressed.jpg)
    27‚Üí
    28‚Üí{:.post-img-credit}
    29‚ÜíPhoto by James Vaughan (CC BY-NC-SA 2.0)
    30‚Üí
    31‚ÜíLast fall, my wife took me to visit Philip Johnson's Glass House in New Caanan,
    32‚ÜíCT. Beautiful and simple, the Glass House is an icon of modern architecture. It
    33‚Üírests on a property filled with Johnson‚Äôs experimental creations, including a
    34‚Üíbunker that houses art by Andy Warhol and Jasper Johns. The house itself is four
    35‚Üíwalls of glass with 360-degree views of the surrounding woods where coyotes howl
    36‚Üíat night. On the property, there's a perilously large staircase that extends to
    37‚Üínowhere, a footbridge that intentionally bounces as you cross a dry creek and a
    38‚Üíhighly toxic cactus that rests on his desk. One of Mr. Johnson's guiding
    39‚Üíprinciples in architecture is the concept of "safe danger"; the idea that we are
    40‚Üímost engaged when we can take risks in a safe environment.
    41‚Üí
    42‚ÜíTesting provides an environment for developers to take risks safely to produce
    43‚Üítheir best work. Each commit comes with a set of assertions that proves that the
    44‚Üínewly added code has been thoughtfully examined. It gives team members the
    45‚Üíability to completely gut the contents of the production code and not lose any
    46‚Üísleep over it. Anybody can rearrange files, rename functions and variables, and
    47‚Üíbreak large pieces down into new abstractions. I can add a new feature and not
    48‚Üíworry about a coworker (or myself in most cases) not understanding the behavior
    49‚Üíat a later date. When a new person joins the company, they feel confident that
    50‚Üíthey will get early feedback that they broke something. Nobody wants to feel set
    51‚Üíup for failure or responsible for the loss of revenue due to a production bug.
    52‚ÜíWith a testing library, we can build an environment that encourages people to
    53‚Üínot only take risks but have fun along the way.
    54‚Üí
    55‚Üí## Confidence and trust
    56‚Üí
    57‚ÜíAt the heart of any team is the ability for members to trust one another to make
    58‚Üíchoices. Teams with low levels of trust inevitably create systems to prevent
    59‚Üípeople from making choices. Bureaucracy takes hold and the innovative spark is
    60‚Üílost as team members begin to feel like they're cogs in a machine. In web
    61‚Üídevelopment, we prize our ability to make choices and we thrive on learning. By
    62‚Üítaking away a developer's ability to think, you take away their ability to make
    63‚Üían impact on a technology stack. Your junior developer today could become the
    64‚Üíperson that creates software that fundamentally changes the business tomorrow,
    65‚Üíbut you need to give that person the room to make mistakes and learn.
    66‚Üí
    67‚ÜíYou build trust between team members and stakeholders by developing a culture
    68‚Üíthat prioritizes testing. Bugs and unintended side effects are minimized. Silly
    69‚Üímistakes are removed and handled before they reach a staging environment.
    70‚ÜíCustomers experience less downtime, management doesn't feel the need to create
    71‚Üíbureaucratic systems, and developers get to try new things.  Nobody loses sleep
    72‚Üíover a deploy, features are shipped, and the team feels confident that they are
    73‚Üímoving fast without causing damage.
    74‚Üí
    75‚Üí## Documentation for free
    76‚Üí
    77‚ÜíLegibility is a side-effect of encapsulating code into testable pieces with
    78‚Üíclear assertions. Legibility gives not only your team members a chance to read
    79‚Üíand understand your intent, but gives you a better understanding when you return
    80‚Üíto code at a later date. Well-written test assertions are a bit like having
    81‚Üíwell-written annotations to a technical blueprint. You get the benefit of
    82‚Üíunderstanding the intent of the behavior, not just a visual understanding of the
    83‚Üímechanics.
    84‚Üí
    85‚ÜíWriting clear documentation is another difficult challenge when working under
    86‚Üístrict deadlines. Oftentimes, projects are made quickly and documentation is
    87‚Üímade later. Developers have to comb through the codebase to determine how the
    88‚Üícode works and what parts need to be communicated. One of the bonuses of testing
    89‚Üíis that behavior is documented in the test suite. Assertions use plain English
    90‚Üíand describe the expected behavior of a specific piece of code. A
    91‚Üíwell-maintained test suite is not a substitute for documentation, but it can
    92‚Üímake the process of writing documentation much faster.
    93‚Üí
    94‚Üí## Red, green, refactor
    95‚Üí
    96‚ÜíTest Driven Development is a recursive set of steps a software developer follows
    97‚Üíto create new features. You write tests first, then write enough code to satisfy
    98‚Üíthe failing test, and lastly, refactor the code you just wrote. Continue that
    99‚Üíprocess until you've completed your work. It's dead simple and effective.
   100‚Üí
   101‚ÜíI adhere to Uncle Bob's [Three Laws of
   102‚ÜíTDD](http://www.butunclebob.com/ArticleS.UncleBob.TheThreeRulesOfTdd){:target="_blank"}:
   103‚Üí
   104‚Üí1. You are not allowed to write any production code unless it is to make a
   105‚Üí   failing unit test pass.
   106‚Üí2. You are not allowed to write any more of a unit test than is sufficient to
   107‚Üí   fail; and compilation failures are failures.
   108‚Üí3. You are not allowed to write any more production code than is sufficient to
   109‚Üí   pass the one failing unit test.
   110‚Üí
   111‚ÜíPeople are usually overwhelmed by this, but it's like riding a bike. Once you get
   112‚Üípast the initial learning curve it becomes second nature.
   113‚Üí
   114‚Üí### A word on "refactoring"
   115‚Üí
   116‚ÜíWhat does refactoring mean? According to [Martin
   117‚ÜíFowler](https://refactoring.com/){:target="_blank"}, "Refactoring is a disciplined technique for
   118‚Üírestructuring an existing body of code, altering its internal structure without
   119‚Üíchanging its external behavior."  The key phrase in this definition is "without
   120‚Üíchanging its external behavior."  Implicit in this definition is confidence and
   121‚Üícertainty. How can you be confident that your changes didn't change external
   122‚Üíbehavior? I posit that the only way you can have certainty is through some form
   123‚Üíof checking, either manually or through automated tests. Changing code without
   124‚Üímeaningful feedback is rewriting, not refactoring.
   125‚Üí
   126‚Üí## Todo list example
   127‚Üí
   128‚ÜíFor the remainder of this post, I will create a series of features for a Todo
   129‚ÜíList Application in React, following Uncle Bob's rules, so you can see the
   130‚Üíchanges over time. The intention is to show how the code changes, the way I
   131‚Üíthink, what I write, and most importantly, what I leave out. I oftentimes see
   132‚Üídevelopers in interviews add more code than they need upfront to address all
   133‚Üípotential edgecases but those concerns aren't important until problems arise. We
   134‚Üídon't want to forecast problems, we want to solve the problems right in front of
   135‚Üíus.
   136‚Üí
   137‚ÜíThe full code base can be seen on [CodeSandbox](http://bit.ly/2IW51qj){:target="_blank"}.
   138‚Üí
   139‚Üí### Create the folder and test file
   140‚Üí
   141‚ÜíThere are different ways to organize your files and folders in a Javascript code
   142‚Üíbase. I create folders for new files with an index to export contents in order
   143‚Üíto co-locate important pieces. The folder gives us a space to create
   144‚Üítest files, css, helpers, or child subcomponent folders.
   145‚Üí
   146‚Üí\```
   147‚Üí/src
   148‚Üí  /App
   149‚Üí    index.js
   150‚Üí    App.css
   151‚Üí    App.jsx
   152‚Üí    App.test.jsx
   153‚Üí\```
   154‚Üí
   155‚ÜíFollowing this pattern, let's create a `TodoList` component folder with a test
   156‚Üífile first.
   157‚Üí
   158‚Üí\```diff
   159‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   160‚Üínew file mode 100644
   161‚Üíindex 0000000..1a6e53f
   162‚Üí--- /dev/null
   163‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   164‚Üí@@ -0,0 +1,10 @@
   165‚Üí+import React from "react";
   166‚Üí+import { render } from "@testing-library/react";
   167‚Üí+
   168‚Üí+import { TodoList } from ".";
   169‚Üí+
   170‚Üí+describe("TodoList", () => {
   171‚Üí+  it("works", () => {
   172‚Üí+    render(<TodoList />);
   173‚Üí+  });
   174‚Üí+});
   175‚Üí\```
   176‚Üí
   177‚ÜíThat's it. That's how you start. Notice that I did not create the `index.js` or
   178‚Üíthe production code in `TodoList.jsx` yet? Run the test suite. This initial test
   179‚Üíshould fail (Red). There are a few important reasons why you want to start every
   180‚Üínew component this way.
   181‚Üí
   182‚Üí1. It establishes the dependencies needed to start testing. I prefer React
   183‚Üí   Testing Library when testing React components to test behavior as a user sees
   184‚Üí   it. By attempting a render, I'm attempting to establish the connection
   185‚Üí   between test file and production code.
   186‚Üí2. It establishes the way I expect to consume the component. By attempting to
   187‚Üí   import directly from the folder, I'm testing that there is an established
   188‚Üí   contract for consuming the new code.
   189‚Üí3. I'm isolating the test suite to just the behavior of the component.
   190‚Üí
   191‚ÜíNow let's make the component and the index file.
   192‚Üí
   193‚Üí\```diff
   194‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   195‚Üínew file mode 100644
   196‚Üíindex 0000000..ad0c714
   197‚Üí--- /dev/null
   198‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   199‚Üí@@ -0,0 +1,5 @@
   200‚Üí+import React from "react";
   201‚Üí+
   202‚Üí+export function TodoList() {
   203‚Üí+  return <div />;
   204‚Üí+}
   205‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/index.js b/src/TodoList/index.js
   206‚Üínew file mode 100644
   207‚Üíindex 0000000..f239f43
   208‚Üí--- /dev/null
   209‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/index.js
   210‚Üí@@ -0,0 +1 @@
   211‚Üí+export * from './TodoList';
   212‚Üí\```
   213‚Üí
   214‚ÜíAgain, that's it. We've now fixed the broken test (Green). It's not much, but
   215‚Üíit's how I start every new isolated module. This could be a React component, it
   216‚Üícould be a Node module, the pattern is the same.
   217‚Üí
   218‚ÜíNow let's start adding meaningful features.
   219‚Üí
   220‚Üí### Giving the user an input
   221‚Üí
   222‚ÜíIn this initial pass, I'm going to attempt to add an input for the user to add
   223‚Üítodos.  I want to be sure that the input takes and shows the values.
   224‚Üí
   225‚Üí\```diff
   226‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   227‚Üíindex 1a6e53f..9151a6e 100644
   228‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   229‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   230‚Üí@@ -1,10 +1,13 @@
   231‚Üí import React from "react";
   232‚Üí-import { render } from "@testing-library/react";
   233‚Üí+import { render, fireEvent } from "@testing-library/react";
   234‚Üí
   235‚Üí import { TodoList } from ".";
   236‚Üí
   237‚Üí describe("TodoList", () => {
   238‚Üí-  it("works", () => {
   239‚Üí-    render(<TodoList />);
   240‚Üí+  it("receives user input", () => {
   241‚Üí+    const { getByTestId } = render(<TodoList />);
   242‚Üí+    const input = getByTestId("todo-input");
   243‚Üí+    fireEvent.change(input, { target: { value: "Take the dinglebop" } });
   244‚Üí+    expect(input.value).toBe("Take the dinglebop");
   245‚Üí   });
   246‚Üí });
   247‚Üí\```
   248‚Üí
   249‚ÜíI'll run the test suite to let it fail and begin fixing the code to make it
   250‚Üípass. After it fails (Red), I'm going to create a simple input that takes user
   251‚Üívalues, set it to an internal state, and render the value in the input.
   252‚Üí
   253‚Üí\```diff
   254‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   255‚Üíindex ad0c714..e9c78bc 100644
   256‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   257‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   258‚Üí@@ -1,5 +1,15 @@
   259‚Üí-import React from "react";
   260‚Üí+import React, { useState } from "react";
   261‚Üí
   262‚Üí export function TodoList() {
   263‚Üí-  return <div />;
   264‚Üí+  const [inputState, inputDispatch] = useState("");
   265‚Üí+  return (
   266‚Üí+    <input
   267‚Üí+      data-testid="todo-input"
   268‚Üí+      type="text"
   269‚Üí+      value={inputState}
   270‚Üí+      onChange={e => {
   271‚Üí+        inputDispatch(e.target.value);
   272‚Üí+      }}
   273‚Üí+    />
   274‚Üí+  );
   275‚Üí }
   276‚Üí\```
   277‚Üí
   278‚ÜíAfter I've added my new code, I'll run the test suite to make it pass (Green). I
   279‚Üíthink this is simple enough that no further refactoring is needed. I'll move
   280‚Üíforward with another set of behavior assertions.
   281‚Üí
   282‚Üí### Saving a todo
   283‚Üí
   284‚ÜíI now want to test the entire user flow of adding text to the input and saving
   285‚Üíit to the list.
   286‚Üí
   287‚Üí\```diff
   288‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   289‚Üíindex 9151a6e..d768b4a 100644
   290‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   291‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   292‚Üí@@ -10,4 +10,15 @@ describe("TodoList", () => {
   293‚Üí     fireEvent.change(input, { target: { value: "Take the dinglebop" } });
   294‚Üí     expect(input.value).toBe("Take the dinglebop");
   295‚Üí   });
   296‚Üí+
   297‚Üí+  it("adds a todo", () => {
   298‚Üí+    const { getByTestId } = render(<TodoList />);
   299‚Üí+    const input = getByTestId("todo-input");
   300‚Üí+    const add = getByTestId("todo-add");
   301‚Üí+    fireEvent.change(input, { target: { value: "Smooth it out with a bunch of shleem" } });
   302‚Üí+    fireEvent.click(add);
   303‚Üí+    const todo = getByTestId("todo");
   304‚Üí+    expect(todo.textContent).toBe("Smooth it out with a bunch of shleem");
   305‚Üí+  });
   306‚Üí });
   307‚Üí\```
   308‚Üí
   309‚ÜíYou'll notice that there is some repetition. That's okay, we want to be sure
   310‚Üíthat we're completely isolating our tests to avoid weird side effects. Do not be
   311‚Üítempted to stick a huge `beforeEach` setup because you want things to be DRY. If
   312‚Üíyou start now, you'll just continue adding things to the block and it will
   313‚Üíbecome unreadable for yourself and other devs over time. Run the test suite
   314‚Üíagain to be sure the test fails (Red).
   315‚Üí
   316‚Üí\```diff
   317‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   318‚Üíindex e9c78bc..b75791b 100644
   319‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   320‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   321‚Üí@@ -1,15 +1,29 @@
   322‚Üí import React, { useState } from "react";
   323‚Üí
   324‚Üí export function TodoList() {
   325‚Üí+  const [todos, updateTodos] = useState([]);
   326‚Üí   const [inputState, inputDispatch] = useState("");
   327‚Üí+  const addTodo = newTodo => updateTodos([...todos, newTodo]);
   328‚Üí   return (
   329‚Üí-    <input
   330‚Üí-      data-testid="todo-input"
   331‚Üí-      type="text"
   332‚Üí-      value={inputState}
   333‚Üí-      onChange={e => {
   334‚Üí-        inputDispatch(e.target.value);
   335‚Üí-      }}
   336‚Üí-    />
   337‚Üí+    <div>
   338‚Üí+      <input
   339‚Üí+        data-testid="todo-input"
   340‚Üí+        type="text"
   341‚Üí+        value={inputState}
   342‚Üí+        onChange={e => {
   343‚Üí+          inputDispatch(e.target.value);
   344‚Üí+        }}
   345‚Üí+      />
   346‚Üí+      <button data-testid="todo-add" onClick={() => addTodo(inputState)}>
   347‚Üí+        Add
   348‚Üí+      </button>
   349‚Üí+      <ul>
   350‚Üí+        {todos.map((todo, index) => (
   351‚Üí+          <li key={index} data-testid="todo">
   352‚Üí+            {todo}
   353‚Üí+          </li>
   354‚Üí+        ))}
   355‚Üí+      </ul>
   356‚Üí+    </div>
   357‚Üí   );
   358‚Üí }
   359‚Üí\```
   360‚Üí
   361‚ÜíI've introduced a new piece of state, a button to add a todo directly from the
   362‚Üíinput state, and a list of todos. I'll run the test suite and see that it
   363‚Üípasses (Green). Now that the tests are passing, let's consider refactoring.
   364‚Üí
   365‚Üí### Refactoring after getting todo's saved
   366‚Üí
   367‚ÜíHere's some things I want to consider changing:
   368‚Üí
   369‚Üí* I don't like the term "inputDispatch" and I actually like the way I named
   370‚Üí    "updateTodos". It feels more declarative and explicit.
   371‚Üí* I know that I could use a reducer but there really isn't a need at this moment
   372‚Üí    to use one. I'll hold off for now.
   373‚Üí
   374‚Üí\```diff
   375‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   376‚Üíindex b75791b..2483839 100644
   377‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   378‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   379‚Üí@@ -2,19 +2,19 @@ import React, { useState } from "react";
   380‚Üí
   381‚Üí export function TodoList() {
   382‚Üí   const [todos, updateTodos] = useState([]);
   383‚Üí-  const [inputState, inputDispatch] = useState("");
   384‚Üí+  const [userInput, updateUserInput] = useState("");
   385‚Üí   const addTodo = newTodo => updateTodos([...todos, newTodo]);
   386‚Üí   return (
   387‚Üí     <div>
   388‚Üí       <input
   389‚Üí         data-testid="todo-input"
   390‚Üí         type="text"
   391‚Üí-        value={inputState}
   392‚Üí+        value={userInput}
   393‚Üí         onChange={e => {
   394‚Üí-          inputDispatch(e.target.value);
   395‚Üí+          updateUserInput(e.target.value);
   396‚Üí         }}
   397‚Üí       />
   398‚Üí-      <button data-testid="todo-add" onClick={() => addTodo(inputState)}>
   399‚Üí+      <button data-testid="todo-add" onClick={() => addTodo(userInput)}>
   400‚Üí         Add
   401‚Üí       </button>
   402‚Üí       <ul>
   403‚Üí\```
   404‚Üí
   405‚ÜíThe changes are minimal but show the process of how we can make changes without
   406‚Üíchanging external behavior. Let's move on to more features.
   407‚Üí
   408‚Üí### Reset the user input after adding a todo
   409‚Üí
   410‚ÜíNow that we're adding todos and rendering them for the user, we want to reset
   411‚Üíthe user input so the user can continue adding more.
   412‚Üí
   413‚Üí\```diff
   414‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   415‚Üíindex f939631..4908af4 100644
   416‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   417‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   418‚Üí@@ -20,4 +20,15 @@ describe("TodoList", () => {
   419‚Üí     const todo = getByTestId("todo");
   420‚Üí     expect(todo.textContent).toBe("Smooth it out with a bunch of shleem");
   421‚Üí   });
   422‚Üí+
   423‚Üí+  it("clears the user input after a todo is added", () => {
   424‚Üí+    const { getByTestId } = render(<TodoList />);
   425‚Üí+    const input = getByTestId("todo-input");
   426‚Üí+    const add = getByTestId("todo-add");
   427‚Üí+    fireEvent.change(input, {
   428‚Üí+      target: { value: "Re-purpose shleem for later batches" }
   429‚Üí+    });
   430‚Üí+    fireEvent.click(add);
   431‚Üí+    expect(input.value).toBe("");
   432‚Üí+  });
   433‚Üí });
   434‚Üí\```
   435‚Üí
   436‚ÜíI'll run the test suite to make it fail (Red).
   437‚Üí
   438‚Üí\```diff
   439‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   440‚Üíindex 2483839..4adf6d6 100644
   441‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   442‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   443‚Üí@@ -14,7 +14,13 @@ export function TodoList() {
   444‚Üí           updateUserInput(e.target.value);
   445‚Üí         }}
   446‚Üí       />
   447‚Üí-      <button data-testid="todo-add" onClick={() => addTodo(userInput)}>
   448‚Üí+      <button
   449‚Üí+        data-testid="todo-add"
   450‚Üí+        onClick={() => {
   451‚Üí+          addTodo(userInput);
   452‚Üí+          updateUserInput("");
   453‚Üí+        }}
   454‚Üí+      >
   455‚Üí         Add
   456‚Üí       </button>
   457‚Üí       <ul>
   458‚Üí\```
   459‚Üí
   460‚ÜíI've now added a function call for `updateUserInput("")` to the button click
   461‚Üíhandler to clear the user input state. However, we still have the issue that users
   462‚Üícan add empty todos to the list. Let's fix that.
   463‚Üí
   464‚Üí### Ensuring todo field isn't empty
   465‚Üí
   466‚Üí\```diff
   467‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   468‚Üíindex 4908af4..04c7a4c 100644
   469‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   470‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   471‚Üí@@ -31,4 +31,10 @@ describe("TodoList", () => {
   472‚Üí     fireEvent.click(add);
   473‚Üí     expect(input.value).toBe("");
   474‚Üí   });
   475‚Üí+
   476‚Üí+  it('disables the "Add Todo" button when the user input is empty', () => {
   477‚Üí+    const { getByTestId } = render(<TodoList />);
   478‚Üí+    const add = getByTestId("todo-add");
   479‚Üí+    expect(add.disabled).toBe(true);
   480‚Üí+  });
   481‚Üí });
   482‚Üí\```
   483‚Üí
   484‚Üí\```diff
   485‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   486‚Üíindex 4adf6d6..a643fee 100644
   487‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   488‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   489‚Üí@@ -16,6 +16,7 @@ export function TodoList() {
   490‚Üí       />
   491‚Üí       <button
   492‚Üí         data-testid="todo-add"
   493‚Üí+        disabled={userInput === "" ? true : false}
   494‚Üí         onClick={() => {
   495‚Üí           addTodo(userInput);
   496‚Üí           updateUserInput("");
   497‚Üí@@ -26,7 +27,7 @@ export function TodoList() {
   498‚Üí       <ul>
   499‚Üí         {todos.map((todo, index) => (
   500‚Üí           <li key={index} data-testid="todo">
   501‚Üí-            {todo}
   502‚Üí+           {todo}
   503‚Üí           </li>
   504‚Üí         ))}
   505‚Üí       </ul>
   506‚Üí\```
   507‚Üí
   508‚ÜíWe now have a comprehensive set of behaviors that we expect from our TodoList
   509‚Üíapplication. There are still a few crucial pieces that need to be addressed --
   510‚Üíediting and deleting. Let's add those features now.
   511‚Üí
   512‚Üí### Delete todos
   513‚Üí
   514‚ÜíI'm going to have to set up a todo, attempt to remove it with a new button that I
   515‚Üíintend to add next to each element, and then check that the todo on the page
   516‚Üíhas been removed. I'll run the test and it should fail because it won't find the
   517‚Üí`todo-remove` button. After fixing that, I'll run it again to be sure that the
   518‚Üítodos are rendering and failing the test as expected.
   519‚Üí
   520‚Üí\```diff
   521‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   522‚Üíindex 04c7a4c..20c35b8 100644
   523‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   524‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.test.jsx
   525‚Üí@@ -37,4 +37,17 @@ describe("TodoList", () => {
   526‚Üí     const add = getByTestId("todo-add");
   527‚Üí     expect(add.disabled).toBe(true);
   528‚Üí   });
   529‚Üí+
   530‚Üí+  it("deletes todos", () => {
   531‚Üí+    const { getByTestId, queryAllByTestId } = render(<TodoList />);
   532‚Üí+    const input = getByTestId("todo-input");
   533‚Üí+    const add = getByTestId("todo-add");
   534‚Üí+    fireEvent.change(input, {
   535‚Üí+      target: { value: "Take the dinglebop and push it through the grumbo" }
   536‚Üí+    });
   537‚Üí+    fireEvent.click(add);
   538‚Üí+    const remove = getByTestId("todo-remove");
   539‚Üí+    fireEvent.click(remove);
   540‚Üí+    expect(queryAllByTestId("todo")).toHaveLength(0);
   541‚Üí+  });
   542‚Üí });
   543‚Üí\```
   544‚Üí
   545‚Üí\```diff
   546‚Üídiff --git a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   547‚Üíindex a643fee..20d40f6 100644
   548‚Üí--- a/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   549‚Üí+++ b/src/TodoList/TodoList.jsx
   550‚Üí@@ -4,6 +4,8 @@ export function TodoList() {
   551‚Üí   const [todos, updateTodos] = useState([]);
   552‚Üí   const [userInput, updateUserInput] = useState("");

   941‚Üí
   942‚Üí## Take home assignment
   943‚Üí
   944‚ÜíIf you visit the Code Sandbox link, you can download the repo and begin testing
   945‚Üíusing the Create React App scripts in the `package.json` file. You'll be able to
   946‚Üípick up right where I left off and begin adding some new features. Here are a few
   947‚Üíthings you could implement:
   948‚Üí
   949‚Üí* Hiding the 'Edit' and 'Remove' controls when the user opens the inline editing experience
   950‚Üí* Turning off the editing experience when the user saves a new input
   951‚Üí* Adding a 'Cancel' button to turn off the editing experience
   952‚Üí
   953‚ÜíI would focus on thinking through how you would set up a new test and making
   954‚Üísure that you have the right failing test. TDD is a skill that you will
   955‚Üícontinually need to practice, learn, and improve. I've benefited greatly in my
   956‚Üíprofessional development by having this tool available in my toolbox. I hope
   957‚Üíthis long form post will serve as a reference for how to start your journey on
   958‚Üítesting.
   959‚Üí

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514) (sidechain)**_

Tool use: **Read** `/Users/anthonygonzales/code/antgonzales.github.io/_posts/2020-05-26-how-to-test-data-fetching-components.md`

```
1‚Üí---
     2‚Üílayout: post
     3‚Üítitle: "Testing components that make API calls"
     4‚Üídescription: "Learn how to test API calls in components with examples in React
     5‚Üíand Jest. Write tests flexible enough for change"
     6‚Üíimage: "post-boxes-on-brick-compressed.jpg"
     7‚Üídate: 2020-05-25
     8‚Üílast_modified_at: 2024-03-03
     9‚Üí---
    10‚Üí
    11‚ÜíMost examples that discuss [Test-Driven
    12‚ÜíDevelopment](https://www.anthonygonzales.dev/blog/why-learn-test-driven-development.html)
    13‚Üídon't include information about how to test components that fetch data. With
    14‚ÜíJest, we get an environment in Node.js that mimics the browser because it
    15‚Üíprovides jsdom. However, Jest does not describe a "batteries included" vision
    16‚Üífor server responses. Let's discuss the best way to test front-end components
    17‚Üíthat make API calls.
    18‚Üí
    19‚Üí* Do not remove this line (it will not be displayed)
    20‚Üí{:toc}
    21‚Üí
    22‚Üí<!--break-->
    23‚Üí
    24‚Üí## Mocks are risky assumptions
    25‚Üí
    26‚ÜíI often see examples advising that you mock an entire library. The examples
    27‚Üímock axios, request, or fetch to test that a specific function is called.
    28‚ÜíHere's an example provided by [Testing
    29‚ÜíLibrary](https://web.archive.org/web/20200512192923/https://testing-library.com/docs/react-testing-library/example-intro/){:
    30‚Üírel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"} using React:
    31‚Üí
    32‚Üí\```jsx
    33‚Üí// fetch/fetch.test.js
    34‚Üíimport React from 'react'
    35‚Üíimport { render, fireEvent, waitFor, screen } from '@testing-library/react'
    36‚Üíimport '@testing-library/jest-dom/extend-expect'
    37‚Üíimport axiosMock from 'axios'
    38‚Üíimport Fetch from '.'
    39‚Üí
    40‚Üíjest.mock('axios')
    41‚Üí
    42‚Üítest('loads and displays greeting', async () => {
    43‚Üí  const url = '/greeting'
    44‚Üí  render(<Fetch url={url} />)
    45‚Üí
    46‚Üí  axiosMock.get.mockResolvedValueOnce({
    47‚Üí    data: { greeting: 'hello there' },
    48‚Üí  })
    49‚Üí
    50‚Üí  fireEvent.click(screen.getByText('Load Greeting'))
    51‚Üí
    52‚Üí  await waitFor(() => screen.getByRole('heading'))
    53‚Üí
    54‚Üí  expect(axiosMock.get).toHaveBeenCalledTimes(1)
    55‚Üí  expect(axiosMock.get).toHaveBeenCalledWith(url)
    56‚Üí  expect(screen.getByRole('heading')).toHaveTextContent('hello there')
    57‚Üí  expect(screen.getByRole('button')).toHaveAttribute('disabled')
    58‚Üí})
    59‚Üí\```
    60‚Üí
    61‚Üí<div class="callout warning-callout">
    62‚ÜíUpdate: Testing Library recommends <a href="https://mswjs.io" re="noopener
    63‚Üínofollow" target="_blank">Mock Service Worker</a> and no longer maintains the
    64‚Üíexample above.
    65‚Üí</div>
    66‚Üí
    67‚ÜíThis approach tests implementation details in addition to behavior. It binds our
    68‚Üítest suite to a library and assumes that the library's API will not change. It
    69‚Üíalso assumes that we're using the library method correctly. In this case, our
    70‚Üítest suite is now bound to axios, and the method `get()`. If your team wants to
    71‚Üíswitch request libraries from axios to another option such as unfetch, the test
    72‚Üíexample above will need to be re-written to account for unfetch's API. Say you
    73‚Üíhave 4k tests on a large project? To properly refactor, you will need to
    74‚Üíre-write all tests that directly mock axios. You will lose your testing baseline
    75‚Üíwhich means you will need to follow Red, Green, Refactor across all of the tests
    76‚Üíyou previously wrote. The process of changing your data fetching library will be
    77‚Üítedious and prone to errors.
    78‚Üí
    79‚Üí
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üí## Which API inteceptor library should I use?
    82‚Üí
    83‚ÜíThere are several libraries available to stub server responses:
    84‚Üí
    85‚Üí* miragejs
    86‚Üí* msw
    87‚Üí* cypress
    88‚Üí* nock
    89‚Üí
    90‚ÜíI recommend [msw](https://mswjs.io/){: rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"} for
    91‚Üíseveral compelling reasons:
    92‚Üí
    93‚Üí* Seamless integration with both browser and Node.js environments
    94‚Üí* Realistic request interception
    95‚Üí* Rich documentation and community support
    96‚Üí
    97‚Üímsw is a powerful tool for mocking API responses in both front-end and back-end
    98‚Üítesting environments, offering seamless integration without the need for
    99‚Üíconfiguring a separate server or altering your production code's network
   100‚Üírequests. This library stands out because it intercepts requests at the network
   101‚Üílevel, allowing for a more realistic simulation of API calls in development and
   102‚Üítesting scenarios.
   103‚Üí
   104‚Üí## Implement a fake server 
   105‚Üí
   106‚ÜíLet's look at msw using the previous example and assume we've already done
   107‚Üíthe recommended setup.
   108‚Üí
   109‚Üí\```jsx
   110‚Üí// fetch/fetch.test.js
   111‚Üíimport React from 'react'
   112‚Üíimport { rest } from 'msw';
   113‚Üíimport { render, fireEvent, waitFor, screen } from '@testing-library/react'
   114‚Üí
   115‚Üíimport { server } from '@/mocks/server';
   116‚Üí
   117‚Üíimport Fetch from '.'
   118‚Üí
   119‚Üítest('override handler in a single test', async () => {
   120‚Üí  // Override the handler for this test
   121‚Üí  server.use(
   122‚Üí    rest.get('https://yoursite.com/greeting', (req, res, ctx) => {
   123‚Üí      return res(ctx.json({ greeting: 'hello there' }));
   124‚Üí    })
   125‚Üí  );
   126‚Üí
   127‚Üí  const url = '/greeting';
   128‚Üí  render(<Fetch url={url} />);
   129‚Üí  fireEvent.click(screen.getByText('Load Greeting'));
   130‚Üí
   131‚Üí  await waitFor(() => screen.getByRole('heading'));
   132‚Üí
   133‚Üí  // Assertions can now expect the overridden behavior
   134‚Üí  expect(screen.getByRole('heading')).toHaveTextContent('hello there');
   135‚Üí  expect(screen.getByRole('button')).toHaveAttribute('disabled');
   136‚Üí});
   137‚Üí\```
   138‚Üí
   139‚ÜíIn the new and immproved approach, we've done several things:
   140‚Üí
   141‚Üí1. Stopped mocking the axios library and method response
   142‚Üí2. Specified a response at a url and a route
   143‚Üí3. Removed unnecessary assertions about API calls
   144‚Üí
   145‚ÜíOur test suite no longer knows the way our components fetch data. If you switch
   146‚Üífrom axios, fetch, or unfetch, the test file will not require changes. More
   147‚Üíimportantly, if you upgrade your data fetching library version, your test suite
   148‚Üíwill give you meaningful feedback. When we mock a dependency, we begin testing
   149‚Üíwith faulty assumptions that the package will not have made breaking changes to
   150‚Üíits internals or its API, leading to false positives in our test suite.
   151‚Üí
   152‚Üí## How to test components using Apollo Client with GraphQL
   153‚Üí
   154‚Üí![Two red mail boxes against a brick wall in the
   155‚ÜíUK](/assets/img/post-boxes-on-brick-compressed.jpg)
   156‚Üí
   157‚Üí{:.post-img-credit}
   158‚ÜíPhoto by [Kristina
   159‚ÜíTripkovic](https://unsplash.com/@tinamosquito?utm_source=unsplash&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=creditCopyText){:
   160‚Üírel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"} on [Unsplash](https://unsplash.com){: rel="nofollow
   161‚Üínoopener" target="_blank"}
   162‚Üí
   163‚ÜíWith the rise of GraphQL, Apollo has made significant strides in writing server
   164‚Üíand client-side libraries to make managing data easier. The trouble comes with
   165‚Üítheir recommended approach to testing UI components that rely on Apollo.
   166‚Üí
   167‚ÜíApollo has created a `MockedProvider` [test
   168‚Üícomponent](https://www.apollographql.com/docs/react/development-testing/testing/){: rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"}
   169‚Üíwhich allows you to test your UI components. They assert that using the live
   170‚ÜíProvider would be unpredictable as it runs against an actual backend. That may
   171‚Üíbe true, but nothing stops us from hijacking the means of communicating with the
   172‚Üíbackend just like we did with the axios example.
   173‚Üí
   174‚ÜíHere are the things I know about interfacing with Apollo and GraphQL:
   175‚Üí
   176‚Üí1. All requests, queries and mutations, use the HTTP POST method. Because
   177‚Üí   GraphQL serves a single resource, the graph, it doesn't follow the REST
   178‚Üí   resources approach in HTTP (GET/PUT/PATCH/DELETE).
   179‚Üí2. Apollo requires an instantiated client which is essentially a config class
   180‚Üí   for setup.
   181‚Üí3. Apollo ensures type names in the resource response.
   182‚Üí
   183‚ÜíI now know about a few details in setting up a proper test:
   184‚Üí
   185‚Üí1. We need to import the real client to be sure I'm hitting the right endpoint
   186‚Üí2. We need to get some stub data from my endpoint
   187‚Üí3. We're going to respond to a post request with the stub data
   188‚Üí
   189‚ÜíFor this example, I will use the free [Pokemon
   190‚Üílist](https://graphql-pokemon.now.sh){: rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"} server, grab some fake data, and query
   191‚Üíagainst it.
   192‚Üí
   193‚Üí\```jsx
   194‚Üíimport React from "react";
   195‚Üíimport { ApolloProvider } from "@apollo/react-hooks";
   196‚Üíimport { render } from "@testing-library/react";
   197‚Üíimport { graphql } from "msw";
   198‚Üí
   199‚Üíimport { client } from "@/api/client";
   200‚Üíimport { server } from "@/mocks/server";
```

    29‚Üíand built resilient architecture while coordinating approximately 50 frontend
    30‚Üíengineers who collectively merged 800 pull requests. The following case study
    31‚Üíoutlines the key strategies that enabled us to successfully deliver this

    35‚Üí

    39‚Üímove forward. The central question became: How could we deliver quickly without
    40‚Üísacrificing quality or confidence?

## Updated Migration Requirements

1. `{:toc}` ‚Üí Astro TOC component
2. `{:target="_blank"}` ‚Üí HTML target attributes  
3. `{:.class-name}` ‚Üí CSS class application
4. `{:rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"}` ‚Üí Multi-attribute links

This is more complex than initially identified. Your custom remark plugin will need to parse and transform all these attribute patterns.

Now I'll create a comprehensive remark plugin that handles all the kramdown attribute patterns we identified:

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_

Tool use: **Write**

```javascript
import { visit } from 'unist-util-visit';

/**
 * Remark plugin to process Kramdown-style attribute syntax
 * Handles: {:target="_blank"}, {:.class-name}, {:toc}, and complex attributes
 */
export function remarkKramdownAttrs() {
  return (tree) => {
    visit(tree, (node, index, parent) => {
      // Handle text nodes that might contain kramdown attribute syntax
      if (node.type === 'text' && node.value) {
        // Check for kramdown attribute patterns
        const kramdownPattern = /\{:([^}]+)\}/g;
        const matches = [...node.value.matchAll(kramdownPattern)];
        
        if (matches.length > 0) {
          // Process each match
          matches.forEach(match => {
            const attributeString = match[1];
            const fullMatch = match[0];
            
            // Handle table of contents
            if (attributeString === 'toc') {
              // Replace {:toc} with a TOC placeholder that Astro can process
              node.value = node.value.replace(fullMatch, '<!-- TOC_PLACEHOLDER -->');
              return;
            }
            
            // Handle CSS class assignment {:.class-name}
            if (attributeString.startsWith('.')) {
              const className = attributeString.substring(1);
              // Find the previous sibling to apply class to
              if (parent && index > 0) {
                const prevSibling = parent.children[index - 1];
                if (prevSibling) {
                  prevSibling.data = prevSibling.data || {};
                  prevSibling.data.hProperties = prevSibling.data.hProperties || {};
                  prevSibling.data.hProperties.className = className;
                }
              }
              // Remove the attribute text
              node.value = node.value.replace(fullMatch, '');
              return;
            }
            
            // Handle link attributes (target, rel, etc.)
            const attributes = parseKramdownAttributes(attributeString);
            if (Object.keys(attributes).length > 0) {
              // Find the previous link node to apply attributes to
              if (parent && index > 0) {
                const prevSibling = parent.children[index - 1];
                if (prevSibling && prevSibling.type === 'link') {
                  prevSibling.data = prevSibling.data || {};
                  prevSibling.data.hProperties = prevSibling.data.hProperties || {};
                  Object.assign(prevSibling.data.hProperties, attributes);
                }
              }
              // Remove the attribute text
              node.value = node.value.replace(fullMatch, '');
            }
          });
          
          // Clean up empty text nodes
          if (node.value.trim() === '') {
            parent.children.splice(index, 1);
          }
        }
      }
      
      // Handle paragraph nodes that might have kramdown attributes on the next line
      if (node.type === 'paragraph' && parent && index < parent.children.length - 1) {
        const nextSibling = parent.children[index + 1];
        if (nextSibling && nextSibling.type === 'paragraph' && 
            nextSibling.children.length === 1 && 
            nextSibling.children[0].type === 'text') {
          
          const text = nextSibling.children[0].value.trim();
          const kramdownPattern = /^\{:([^}]+)\}$/;
          const match = text.match(kramdownPattern);
          
          if (match) {
            const attributeString = match[1];
            
            // Handle CSS class assignment
            if (attributeString.startsWith('.')) {
              const className = attributeString.substring(1);
              node.data = node.data || {};
              node.data.hProperties = node.data.hProperties || {};
              node.data.hProperties.className = className;
              
              // Remove the attribute paragraph
              parent.children.splice(index + 1, 1);
            }
          }
        }
      }
    });
  };
}

/**
 * Parse kramdown attribute string into an object
 * Example: 'target="_blank" rel="nofollow"' -> {target: "_blank", rel: "nofollow"}
 */
function parseKramdownAttributes(attributeString) {
  const attributes = {};
  
  // Handle simple patterns like target="_blank"
  const attrPattern = /(\w+)=["']([^"']+)["']/g;
  let match;
  
  while ((match = attrPattern.exec(attributeString)) !== null) {
    const [, key, value] = match;
    attributes[key] = value;
  }
  
  return attributes;
}
```

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_

Tool use: **Write**

```javascript
import { visit } from 'unist-util-visit';

/**
 * Remark plugin to handle Jekyll-style <!--break--> excerpt separation
 * Splits content into excerpt and full content based on <!--break--> marker
 */
export function remarkExcerpt() {
  return (tree, file) => {
    let excerptNodes = [];
    let fullContentNodes = [];
    let breakFound = false;
    
    // Walk through all top-level nodes
    tree.children.forEach((node, index) => {
      // Check for HTML comment nodes that contain "break"
      if (node.type === 'html' && node.value.includes('<!--break-->')) {
        breakFound = true;
        return;
      }
      
      // Add to appropriate array based on whether we've found the break
      if (!breakFound) {
        excerptNodes.push(node);
      }
      fullContentNodes.push(node);
    });
    
    // If we found a break, store the excerpt in file data
    if (breakFound && excerptNodes.length > 0) {
      file.data = file.data || {};
      file.data.astro = file.data.astro || {};
      file.data.astro.frontmatter = file.data.astro.frontmatter || {};
      
      // Create a new tree with just the excerpt nodes
      const excerptTree = {
        type: 'root',
        children: excerptNodes
      };
      
      // Store the excerpt tree for later use
      file.data.excerpt = excerptTree;
      file.data.hasExcerpt = true;
    } else {
      file.data = file.data || {};
      file.data.hasExcerpt = false;
    }
  };
}

/**
 * Utility function to render excerpt as HTML (for use in Astro components)
 */
export function getExcerptHTML(file) {
  if (!file.data?.excerpt) {
    return '';
  }
  
  // You would use this with a markdown processor to convert the excerpt tree to HTML
  // This is a placeholder - in Astro, you'd typically use the content renderer
  return file.data.excerpt;
}
```

Instead of doing a direct migration of the previous breaks, is there another system we can use instead?

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_

Yes! Instead of migrating Jekyll's `<!--break-->` system, we can use Astro's built-in content collection features which provide a much cleaner approach:

## Better Astro-Native Excerpt Options

### Option 1: **Frontmatter Excerpt Field** (Recommended)
```yaml
---
title: "Post Title"
description: "This becomes the excerpt"
excerpt: "Custom excerpt text that's separate from description"
---
```

### Option 2: **Astro's Built-in Description Field**
```yaml
---
title: "Post Title" 
description: "This serves as both meta description and excerpt"
---
```

### Option 3: **First Paragraph Auto-Excerpt**
Astro can automatically use the first paragraph as excerpt without any markers.

### Option 4: **Custom Excerpt Length**
Set a character/word limit and auto-truncate content.

## Benefits Over `<!--break-->`

1. **Cleaner content** - No HTML comments in markdown
2. **Better SEO** - Dedicated description field for meta tags
3. **More flexible** - Can have different excerpt vs meta description
4. **Astro-native** - Uses content collection features properly
5. **Easier editing** - Excerpt visible in frontmatter

## Migration Strategy

For your existing posts with `<!--break-->`, we can:
1. Extract text before `<!--break-->` 
2. Add it as `excerpt:` in frontmatter
3. Remove `<!--break-->` markers
4. Keep full content intact

Which approach appeals to you? The frontmatter excerpt field (#1) is most flexible and follows modern static site patterns.

```typescript
import { defineCollection, z } from 'astro:content';

const blog = defineCollection({
  type: 'content',
  schema: z.object({
    title: z.string(),
    description: z.string(),
    date: z.coerce.date(),
    last_modified_at: z.coerce.date().optional(),
    layout: z.string().optional().default('post'),
    redirect_from: z.array(z.string()).optional(),
    draft: z.boolean().optional().default(false),
  }),
});

export const collections = {
  blog,
};
```

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_

Now let me create the blog post layout:

---

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_

Tool use: **Write**

```astro
---
import BaseLayout from './BaseLayout.astro';
import type { CollectionEntry } from 'astro:content';

interface Props {
  post: CollectionEntry<'blog'>;
}

const { post } = Astro.props;
const { data, slug } = post;

function formatDate(date: Date): string {
  return date.toLocaleDateString('en-US', {
    year: 'numeric',
    month: 'long',
    day: 'numeric'
  });
}

const editUrl = `https://github.com/antgonzales/antgonzales.github.io/edit/master/_posts/${slug}.md`;
---

<BaseLayout 
  title={data.title} 
  description={data.description}
  pageClass="post"
>
  <div class="max-width container post" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
    <h1 class="post-title" itemprop="headline">{data.title}</h1>
    <div class="post-meta">
      <span class="hidden" itemprop="author">by Anthony Gonzales</span>
      <time class="post-timestamp" itemprop="datePublished">{formatDate(data.date)}</time>

      {data.last_modified_at && (
        <>
          <span class="post-meta-separator">&bull;</span>
          <div class="post-lastupdated">
            Updated on <time itemprop="dateModified">{formatDate(data.last_modified_at)}</time>
          </div>
        </>
      )}
    </div>

    <div class="post-content" itemprop="articleBody">
      <slot />
    </div>
    <div class="post-additional">
      <a href={editUrl} target="_blank">Suggest a correction</a>
    </div>
  </div>
</BaseLayout>
```

```astro
---
import { type CollectionEntry, getCollection } from 'astro:content';
import PostLayout from '../../layouts/PostLayout.astro';

export async function getStaticPaths() {
  const posts = await getCollection('blog');
  return posts.map((post) => ({
    params: { slug: post.slug },
    props: post,
  }));
}

type Props = CollectionEntry<'blog'>;

const post = Astro.props;
const { Content } = await post.render();
---

<PostLayout post={post}>
  <Content />
</PostLayout>
```

```
1‚Üíimport { visit } from 'unist-util-visit';
     2‚Üí
     3‚Üí/**
     4‚Üí * Remark plugin to process Kramdown-style attribute syntax
     5‚Üí * Handles: {:target="_blank"}, {:.class-name}, {:toc}, and complex attributes
     6‚Üí */
     7‚Üíexport function remarkKramdownAttrs() {
     8‚Üí  return (tree) => {
     9‚Üí    visit(tree, (node, index, parent) => {
    10‚Üí      // Handle text nodes that might contain kramdown attribute syntax
    11‚Üí      if (node.type === 'text' && node.value) {
    12‚Üí        // Check for kramdown attribute patterns
    13‚Üí        const kramdownPattern = /\{:([^}]+)\}/g;
    14‚Üí        const matches = [...node.value.matchAll(kramdownPattern)];
    15‚Üí        
    16‚Üí        if (matches.length > 0) {
    17‚Üí          // Process each match
    18‚Üí          matches.forEach(match => {
    19‚Üí            const attributeString = match[1];
    20‚Üí            const fullMatch = match[0];
    21‚Üí            
    22‚Üí            // Handle table of contents
    23‚Üí            if (attributeString === 'toc') {
    24‚Üí              // Replace {:toc} with a TOC placeholder that Astro can process
    25‚Üí              node.value = node.value.replace(fullMatch, '<!-- TOC_PLACEHOLDER -->');
    26‚Üí              return;
    27‚Üí            }
    28‚Üí            
    29‚Üí            // Handle CSS class assignment {:.class-name}
    30‚Üí            if (attributeString.startsWith('.')) {
```

     3‚Üí/**
     4‚Üí * Remark plugin to process Kramdown-style attribute syntax
     5‚Üí * Handles: {:target="_blank"}, {:.class-name}, {:toc}, and complex attributes
     6‚Üí */
     7‚Üíexport function remarkKramdownAttrs() {
     8‚Üí  return (tree) => {
     9‚Üí    visit(tree, (node, index, parent) => {
    10‚Üí      // Handle paragraphs that contain links followed by kramdown attributes
    11‚Üí      if (node.type === 'paragraph' && node.children) {
    12‚Üí        for (let i = 0; i < node.children.length; i++) {
    13‚Üí          const child = node.children[i];
    14‚Üí          
    15‚Üí          // Look for text nodes with kramdown attributes
    16‚Üí          if (child.type === 'text' && child.value) {
    17‚Üí            const kramdownPattern = /\{:([^}]+)\}/g;
    18‚Üí            const matches = [...child.value.matchAll(kramdownPattern)];
    19‚Üí            
    20‚Üí            if (matches.length > 0) {
    21‚Üí              matches.forEach(match => {
    22‚Üí                const attributeString = match[1];
    23‚Üí                const fullMatch = match[0];
    24‚Üí                
    25‚Üí                // Handle table of contents
    26‚Üí                if (attributeString === 'toc') {
    27‚Üí                  child.value = child.value.replace(fullMatch, '<!-- TOC_PLACEHOLDER -->');
    28‚Üí                  return;
    29‚Üí                }
    30‚Üí                
    31‚Üí                // Handle CSS class assignment {:.class-name}
    32‚Üí                if (attributeString.startsWith('.')) {
    33‚Üí                  const className = attributeString.substring(1);
    34‚Üí                  // Apply to the current paragraph
    35‚Üí                  node.data = node.data || {};
    36‚Üí                  node.data.hProperties = node.data.hProperties || {};
    37‚Üí                  node.data.hProperties.className = className;
    38‚Üí                  child.value = child.value.replace(fullMatch, '');
    39‚Üí                  return;
    40‚Üí                }
    41‚Üí                
    42‚Üí                // Handle link attributes (target, rel, etc.)
    43‚Üí                const attributes = parseKramdownAttributes(attributeString);
    44‚Üí                if (Object.keys(attributes).length > 0) {
    45‚Üí                  // Find the nearest link in this paragraph
    46‚Üí                  for (let j = i - 1; j >= 0; j--) {
    47‚Üí                    const prevChild = node.children[j];
    48‚Üí                    if (prevChild.type === 'link') {
    49‚Üí                      prevChild.data = prevChild.data || {};
    50‚Üí                      prevChild.data.hProperties = prevChild.data.hProperties || {};
    51‚Üí                      Object.assign(prevChild.data.hProperties, attributes);
    52‚Üí                      break;
    53‚Üí                    }
    54‚Üí                  }
    55‚Üí                  child.value = child.value.replace(fullMatch, '');
    56‚Üí                }
    57‚Üí              });
    58‚Üí              
    59‚Üí              // Clean up empty text nodes
    60‚Üí              if (child.value.trim() === '') {
    61‚Üí                node.children.splice(i, 1);
    62‚Üí                i--; // Adjust index after removal
    63‚Üí              }
    64‚Üí            }
    65‚Üí          }
    66‚Üí        }
    67‚Üí      }
    68‚Üí      
    69‚Üí      // Handle paragraph nodes that might have kramdown attributes on the next line
    70‚Üí      if (node.type === 'paragraph' && parent && index < parent.children.length - 1) {
    71‚Üí        const nextSibling = parent.children[index + 1];
```

_**User**_

Before we proceed with Phase 3, I had some thoughts about our approach to Kramdown tags and parsing. Instead of utilizing custom plugins and maintaining the Kramdown syntax, can we come up with different solutions? 1. Is there an Astro plugin for Table of Contents? 2. Should we convert the Kramdown link tags to normal HTML anchor tags instead since Markdown doesn't natively and target="_blank" is a security risk, can we we use https://github.com/rehypejs/rehype-external-links?

---

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_

Excellent suggestions! You're absolutely right - maintaining custom kramdown syntax adds unnecessary complexity. Let's use established Astro/rehype solutions instead.

## Better Approach: Use Standard Plugins

### 1. **Table of Contents**
Yes! Astro has excellent TOC solutions:
- `@astrojs/starlight` has built-in TOC
- `remark-toc` (already installed) generates TOC automatically
- Custom Astro component using `getHeadings()` from content collections

### 2. **External Links**
Perfect! `rehype-external-links` is the standard solution:
- Automatically adds `target="_blank"` and `rel="noopener noreferrer"` to external links
- Security-focused (prevents `window.opener` attacks)
- Zero maintenance vs our custom parser

## Migration Plan

**Instead of kramdown processing:**
1. **Remove our custom remark plugin**
2. **Install `rehype-external-links`** for automatic external link handling
3. **Replace `{:toc}` markers** with Astro's native `getHeadings()` API
4. **Remove `{:.class-name}` patterns** and use proper CSS/components

**Benefits:**
- ‚úÖ Standard, well-maintained plugins
- ‚úÖ Better security (proper `rel` attributes)  
- ‚úÖ Less custom code to maintain
- ‚úÖ More predictable behavior
- ‚úÖ Astro-native TOC generation

## Implementation

Replace our complex kramdown parser with:
```bash
npm install rehype-external-links
```

```js
// astro.config.mjs
rehypePlugins: [
  rehypeSlug,
  [rehypeExternalLinks, { target: '_blank', rel: 'noopener noreferrer' }]
]
```

Should we proceed with this cleaner approach? I can remove the kramdown plugin and implement the standard solutions.

---

_**User**_

Let's proceed with the cleaner approach.

_**Agent (claude-sonnet-4-20250514)**_
